Kaiser Permanente Washington Defined Benefit Plan
Supplement to the Kaiser Permanente Retirement Plan

The Plan is closed to entry by new participants. This section describes conditions of eligibility to become a new
participant that applied before the Plan was closed to new entry. It also describes conditions when an employee who
became a participant before the effective date may cease to earn additional accruals as an "active participant."
To "actively participate" in the Plan means that the individual is a participant in the Plan, is enrolled in the Plan, and
is currently accruing retirement benefits under the Plan. If you are unsure whether or not you actively participate in the
Plan, please contact the Plan administrator.
Kaiser Foundation Health Plan of Washington ("KFHPW") provides a valuable benefit to help you plan for a
secure future - the Kaiser Permanente Washington Defined Benefit Plan (formerly the Retirement Income Credit
Plan for Employees of Group Health Cooperative).

Who Is Eligible

If you were an employee represented by SEIU Healthcare 1199NW before February 9, 2016, you were eligible to
become a participant if you met the following conditions:
Ě You were at least age 21, and
Ě You had one year of eligibility service.
One year of eligibility service means at least 1,000 hours of service in the 12-consecutive-month period
beginning on your date of hire or in any calendar year following your date of hire and before February 9, 2016. If
you transferred from one employer within KFHPW to another, special eligibility provisions may have applied.
Please contact the Plan Administrator for details.
In general, you are in a group covered by this Plan (in other words, in an eligible position) if you do not fall within
a class of staff members who are not eligible (see the Who Is Not Eligible), you are covered by a collective
bargaining agreement that expressly provides for your active participation in the Plan, and you became an active
participant in the Plan before February 9, 2016.

Who Is Not Eligible

The following individuals were not eligible to become a participant in the Plan prior to the Plan becoming closed
to new participants, nor to actively participate in this Plan (to actively participate in the Plan means that the
individual is a Participant in the Plan who is enrolled in and is currently accruing retirement benefits under the
Plan):
Ě Employees who were not participants in the Plan on December 31, 1997 (in other words, did not enroll in the

  Plan before January 1, 1998), unless they are a member of a collective bargaining unit whose collective
  bargaining agreement expressly provides for their active participation in the Plan
Ě Employees of any Permanente Medical Group entity, including Washington Permanente Medical Group,
  formerly Group Health Permanente (GHP), except as described below
Ě Employees of Group Health Options, Inc. (GHO), except as described below
Ě Employees of KPS Health Plans, Inc.
Ě Employees of any Kaiser Permanente entity, except KFHPW, formerly Group Health Cooperative (GHC)

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 68
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Ě Union-represented employees whose employment is governed by a collective bargaining agreement that does not
  provide for their eligibility to participate in this Plan including, without limitation:
     - Employee who received, pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement, a one-time (or final) opportunity to
     choose whether to participate in this Plan or the Group Health Cooperative Employee Defined Contribution
     Plan and who did not choose to participate in this Plan
     - GHC employees in the Pharmacy and Optical bargaining units
     - GHC Eastern Washington/North Idaho employees in the job classifications of consulting nurse,
     team/registered nurse, and registered nurse/oncology who were hired after March 20, 2003
     - GHC Eastern Washington/North Idaho employees in the job classifications of team assistant, medical
     assistant, licensed practical nurse, and courier who were hired after February 23, 2005
     - GHC Eastern Washington/North Idaho employees in the job classifications of masters level therapist,
     chemical dependency therapist, and behavioral health access specialist who were hired after March 20, 2003

Ě Leased employees
Ě Nonresident aliens working outside the United States
Ě Employees whose services are performed outside the United States, unless their principal base of operations to

  which they frequently return is within the United States.
Also, before July 1, 2009, temporary employees, including on-call and interim-assignment employees, were not
eligible to participate in the Plan (except former participants who were rehired on or after January 1, 2002 on a
temporary basis, temporary employees who satisfied the one year of eligibility service requirement described above
or transferees who are active Plan participants when they are transferred).

Participants Who Are Members of Groups Formerly Covered by this Plan

Before January 1, 2012, employees of GHP were eligible to actively participate in this Plan if they: (1) were a
GHC employee and active Plan participant on or after December 31, 1997, (2) were not eligible to participate in
the Group Health Permanente Pension Plan, and (3) were not a highly compensated employee under IRS rules.
Effective January 1, 2012, staff members of GHP are not eligible to actively participate in the Plan.
Before January 1, 2014, certain non-union employees of GHC and GHO, were eligible to actively participate in
the Plan if they were employed with Group Health and actively participating in the Plan on December 31, 1991
or were covered by a collective bargaining agreement that provided for their participation and were actively
participating and accruing a benefit in the Plan before January 1, 2002, and then on or after January 1, 2002,
were transferred or rehired into a position that was not covered by a collective bargaining agreement that
participates in this Plan. Effective January 1, 2014, all non-union employees of GHC and GHO, are not eligible
to actively participate in the Plan.
An individual in either of these groups who became ineligible to actively participate in the Plan after a period
during which he or she was actively participating in the Plan is a Participant in the Plan with respect to the
period(s) of time during which he or she was actively participating in the Plan, until his or her termination of
employment or, if later, he or she receives all benefits, if any, to which he or she is entitled under the Plan.

If You Are Rehired

If you are a rehired employee, your eligibility for participation in the Plan depends on several factors, as described
below:

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 69
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Before January 1, 2002, generally, if you had previously participated in the Plan, you terminated employment,
and you were rehired before January 1, 2002 in a position not covered by a collective bargaining agreement that
provides for your participation in the Plan, then you did not resume active participation in the Plan upon rehire.
Beginning January 1, 2002, and through December 31, 2013, if you were an active participant in the Plan and
you terminated employment, you did not participate in the Defined Contribution Plan before January 1, 2002,
and you were rehired by GHC on or after January 1, 2002 in a position not covered by a collective bargaining
agreement that provided for your participation in the Plan, then you automatically resumed active participation in
the Plan upon rehire. This provision does not apply after December 31, 2013, when non-union staff members are
not eligible to actively participate in the Plan.
Beginning on the Effective Date applicable for Bargaining Units as shown below:
Ě OPEIU Bargaining Unit - February 1, 2016

Ě SEIU Bargaining Unit - February 9, 2016

Ě UFCW ProTech Bargaining Unit - January 29, 2016.

If you are laid off while you were an Active Participant in the KPWA-DB plan and are later rehired into an
Eligible Bargaining Unit Position within 12 months of being laid off, your participation in the KPWA-DB plan
will be automatically reinstated.
If as an Active Participant in the plan, you transfer into a non-Eligible Bargaining Unit position and within 12
months you transfer back to an Eligible Bargaining Unit Position, your participation in the KPWA-DB plan may
be reinstated, provided you give the National Human Resources Service Center (NHRSC) written notification of
your desire to be reinstated in the plan within 30 days of the transfer.

Employees Who Transfer Among Kaiser Permanente Entities

If you transfer to another Kaiser Permanente entity other than KFHPW, you will no longer be eligible to accrue
additional benefits under the Plan. The terms of retirement plans offered by Kaiser Permanente, including pension
plans similar to this Plan, are not uniform. If you transfer jobs with your employer, or if you transfer among
Kaiser Permanente entities during your career, you might participate in different retirement plans and the terms of
those plans may differ significantly. Keep this in mind, and if you transfer, review the Summary Plan Description
for the terms of each retirement plan.

When Your Participation Began

Participation in the Plan began automatically on the first entry date (January 1 or July 1) after you satisfied the
Plan's eligibility requirements provided that you chose, during your DB/DC Election Period, to participate in this
Plan. The DB/DC Election Period was a time period established by Group Health Cooperative during which an
eligible staff member was able to choose whether to participate in this Plan or the Group Health Cooperative
Employee Defined Contribution Plan (the "DC Plan").
Before those dates, Staff who satisfied the eligibility requirements had to actively enroll in the Plan in order to
begin participation as of the next entry date. Staff who were eligible to enroll in the Plan but failed to enroll did
not become participants and did not earn any Plan benefits, nor did they earn any vesting service for calendar years
in which they could have but did not participate.

Beneficiaries

A beneficiary is the individual who may become entitled to benefits under the Plan if you die. You should name a
beneficiary for both your Pension Benefit and your After-tax 2 Percent Account (if any), particularly if you are
unmarried. You can change your beneficiary designation and name a new beneficiary at any time before the date

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 70
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

your benefit payments begin (subject to the requirement for spousal consent if you are married). Please take a
moment to make sure that you have designated a beneficiary, particularly if you are unmarried.
If you are married, your spouse will automatically be your beneficiary unless you elect otherwise with your spouse's
consent. To name someone other than your spouse as beneficiary requires your spouse's written consent, witnessed
by a Plan representative or notary public. If you are legally married, each designation of a new non-spouse
beneficiary requires a new spousal consent.
You can update your beneficiary designation on the Plan administrator's website or by calling the HR Service
Center to have a beneficiary designation form sent to you.

Revisit Your Beneficiary Election When You Reach Age 35

If you are married and name a non-spouse beneficiary before the year in which you reach age 35, your beneficiary
will automatically revert back to your spouse on January 1 of that year. To re-designate a non-spouse beneficiary,
you must complete a new beneficiary form, again with your spouse's written consent.

If No Beneficiary Is Named

If you die with a vested benefit for your Pension Benefit and/or After-tax 2 Percent Account balance but either do
not have a valid beneficiary form for this Plan on file with the external administrator or your designated
beneficiaries do not survive you, your beneficiary(ies) will be the person(s) surviving you in the first of the
following classes in which there is at least one survivor:
Ě Your spouse or domestic partner (as long as, before your death, either: (1) your domestic partnership is

  state-registered, or (2) you have a valid affidavit of domestic partnership on file with the Plan; to submit an
  affidavit of domestic partnership, contact the external administrator)
Ě Your children, except that if any children predecease you but have surviving children of their own, those
  grandchildren will have a right to a pro rata portion of their parents' share
Ě Your parents
Ě Your brothers and sisters, except that if any of your brothers and sisters predecease you but have children of
  their own, those children will have a right to a pro rata portion of their parents' share
Ě Your grandparents
Ě Your aunts and uncles, except that if any of your aunts and uncles predecease you but have children of their
  own, those children will have a right to a pro rata portion of their parents' share
Ě Your estate's executor or administrator.
If you previously made pretax contributions to the 2 Percent Retirement Plan - now part of the Kaiser Permanente
Washington 403(b) Plan (formerly called the Group Health Cooperative 403(b)(7) Custodial Plan) - you must
separately designate a beneficiary under that plan. Please refer to the Kaiser Permanente Washington 403(b)
Plan section for more information.

How the Pension Benefit Works

The Plan provides a traditional defined benefit (DB) Pension Benefit that is calculated based on your years of
participation and earnings during those years. When you retire, this Pension Benefit provides monthly income
during your retirement years. The Pension Benefit is funded entirely by KFHPW.
Unless you elect a different form of payment, the Plan provides monthly payments for your lifetime (with a
survivor pension for your spouse/domestic partner, if any). The amount of your benefit will depend on:

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 71
                 RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Ě The number of years you actively participate in the Plan
Ě Your earnings during that period
Ě Your age when you begin receiving benefits
Ě Your vested percentage (see below)
Ě The benefit payment option you choose.
The Plan also pays a benefit to your spouse/domestic partner (or designated beneficiary if you have no
spouse/domestic partner) if you're vested in the Plan but die before your benefit payments begin.

Vesting in Your Benefit

Vesting means ownership of, or the right to receive, a Plan benefit. You become vested in the Pension Benefit
gradually as you accumulate vesting service under the Plan, as follows:

Vesting Service  Vested Percentage
      3 years          50 percent
      4 years          60 percent
      5 years          70 percent
      6 years          80 percent
      7 years          100 percent

Note: If you terminated employment with KFHPW before January 1, 1989 with only 7 years of vesting service and did
not accumulate additional vesting service following a rehire, you are only 90 percent vested in your Plan benefit.

In addition, you will automatically become 100 percent vested if you are employed by KFHPW when you reach
age 65 or, if earlier, when you die or become eligible for disability retirement (while employed by KFHPW).

You will be eligible to receive a full retirement benefit when you are 100 percent vested. If your employment ends
after you have completed 3 years of vesting service but before you are fully vested, you are eligible for a partial
retirement benefit. See the Vested Termination section.

You earn one year of vesting service for each calendar year in which you complete one or more hours of service.
You are credited with an hour of service for each hour for which you're paid for performance of your duties, or
during vacation, holiday or sick leave or certain other paid leaves.

However, you did not earn vesting service credit for calendar years when you were eligible to participate in the
Plan for the entire calendar year and would have been required to make the 2 percent contribution upon
enrollment, but chose not to enroll.

If you have experienced breaks in service, your years of vesting service prior to the breaks, in very rare
circumstances, may not be taken into account.

How Your Pension Benefit Can Grow

Prior to January 1, 2017: You earn a retirement income credit for each calendar year in which you actively
participate in the Plan.

Beginning January 1, 2017: You earn a retirement income credit for each calendar year in which you actively
participate in the Plan and earn at least 500 hours of service in that calendar year. There is no exception to this
500 hours rule, including, without limitation, for termination as a result of death or disability. Also, hours of
service worked in December but paid in January will be credited in January.

KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 72
       RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

The credit is equal to 2.6 percent of your certified earnings for that calendar year. All of the retirement income
credits you earn during your career with KFHPW are added together and your monthly pension income (in the
form of a single life annuity) starting at age 65 is based on the total of all your credits, multiplied by your vested
percentage (50 percent to 100 percent, depending on your years of vesting service), and divided by 12 to get the
monthly amount. This formula is modified if you begin receiving benefits before age 65 or if you continue
working for KFHPW past age 65.

Certified earnings are your regular base pay, any pretax elective deferrals to a 401(k), 403(b) or 125 cafeteria
plan, and any commissions or incentive pay. Certified earnings do not include overtime pay, bonuses, awards,
stipends or extra pay (such as shift differential, premium pay, call-back, stand-by and temporary relief, special
service and supervisory relief). They also do not include compensation you receive before you start actively
participating in the Plan. For example, if you had entered the Plan on July 1 of a calendar year, earnings you
received between January 1 and June 30 of that year would not have been considered certified earnings.

Example of How Your Pension Benefits Can Grow

This example shows how your Pension Benefit can grow. Anne participates in the Plan from 1997 through 2016,
a 20-year period. Her certified earnings and the credits she earned toward her Pension Benefit each year are shown
in the table:

Year   Certified earnings    X                 = Retirement Income Credits

1997             $22,980   0.026                                  $597.48
1998             $23,664   0.026                                  $615.26
1999             $24,372   0.026                                  $633.67
2000             $25,104   0.026                                  $652.70
2001             $25,860   0.026                                  $672.36
2002             $26,640   0.026                                  $692.64
2003             $27,444   0.026                                  $713.54
2004             $28,272   0.026                                  $735.07
2005             $29,124   0.026                                  $757.22
2006             $30,000   0.026                                  $780.00
2007             $30,900   0.026                                  $803.40
2008             $31,824   0.026                                  $827.42
2009             $32,784   0.026                                  $852.38
                 $33,768   0.026                                  $877.97
2010

2011   $34,776             0.026                                $904.18
2012   $35,820             0.026                                $931.32
2013   $36,900             0.026                                $959.40
2014   $38,004             0.026                                $988.10
2015   $39,144             0.026                               $1,017.74
2016   $40,320             0.026                               $1,048.32

Total                                                          $16,060.17

The total of Anne's retirement income credits are multiplied by her vested percentage, then divided by 12 to get
her monthly Pension Benefit:

       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 73
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

                                       $16,060.17 (sum of retirement income credits)
                                                                  x

                                             100 percent (vested percentage)/12
                                                                  =

                                                                   $1,338.35
So far, based on her 20 years of Plan participation, Anne has earned a Pension Benefit of $1,338.35 per month,
payable for her lifetime in the form of a single life annuity, if she starts pension payments at age 65 (and if she
doesn't earn any more credits).
Please note: the retirement income credits you earn each year do not add up to an account balance. Instead, each
credit is actually a piece of your future annuity benefit. This means that the total of all the credits, multiplied by
your vested percentage and divided by 12, is your monthly pension income payable for life, if you retire at age 65
under the single life annuity option. The amount of your monthly benefit is adjusted if you retire before or after
normal retirement age or choose a different form of payment when you retire. See Your Benefit Payment
Options for more details.

When You Can Begin Your Benefit

If you are vested, you may qualify to begin receiving your benefit at Normal Retirement, Late Retirement, Vested
Termination (including starting the vested portion of your benefits as early as age 55), or Disability Retirement.
Your benefits must begin by April 1 of the year following the year you reach age 72 or terminate employment with
all Kaiser Permanente entities, whichever is later.
However if you are employed by any Kaiser Permanente entity past age 65 and, due to actuarial increases in your
benefit, your benefit amount reaches the maximum amount permitted under the Internal Revenue Code, your
benefits will commence at that time even though you are still employed by a Kaiser Permanente entity.
If you terminate employment with all Kaiser Permanente entities and the present value of your vested benefit is
$1,000 or less (or $5,000 or less if either you are age 65 or older, or if the benefit is payable to a beneficiary, or
alternate payee), your benefit will automatically be distributed in a lump-sum cash distribution, unless you (or the
beneficiary or alternate payee) request a different distribution option such as a direct rollover within 60 days after
being notified of the available payment options, or unless otherwise provided in a qualified domestic relations
order. See Required Distribution of Small Benefits.
You are not eligible to receive Plan benefits while you are receiving or eligible to receive disability benefits provided
by Kaiser Permanente (including short-term disability benefits paid by Kaiser Permanente and long-term disability
benefits received through a Kaiser Permanente provided long-term disability plan, unless (effective January 1,
2013) you are age 55 or over).
Long Term Disability (LTD) insurance contracts, including the one between any Kaiser Permanente entity and its
LTD insurance carrier, often allow the insurance carrier to "offset" (reduce) LTD benefit payments by the amount
of retirement benefits you elect to receive, including benefits from an employer-sponsored pension plan.
If you are receiving or planning to apply for LTD benefits, you should contact the insurance carrier to understand
how those benefits may be reduced if you receive (or begin to receive) benefits from this Plan.

Normal Retirement

The monthly amount you receive may vary depending on the form of payment you choose. Normal retirement
benefits may begin as of the first day of the month following your 65th birthday (provided you have terminated

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 74
                      RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

employment and notified the external administrator of your intention to retire at least 60 days before your normal
retirement date).

Postponed Retirement

If you continue to work for KFHPW past age 65, you are eligible for postponed retirement benefits when your
employment ends. Your monthly pension will begin as of the first day of the next month after termination of
employment (provided you have notified the external administrator of your intention to retire at least 60 days
before your benefit commencement date).

Your benefit will be a monthly amount equal to:

Ě Your accrued monthly pension as of your 65th birthday (your Normal Retirement Benefit)

PLUS

Ě For each plan year you work after your 65th birthday, you will receive the greater of: (1) the amount of your
accrued monthly pension you earn for the current Year of Active Participation, if any, or (2) the annual actuarial
increase on your accrued monthly pension accrued as of the end of the prior plan year. Your benefit will be
prorated based on the number of months worked.

If You Reached Age 65 Before January 1, 2017
If you turned 65 before January 1, 2017, a different formula is used to determine your benefit through December
31, 2016. Your monthly pension through December 31, 2016 is increased using these adjustment factors to reflect
the fact that payments started later:

                  Postponed Retirement Adjustment Factors

Your age  Factor for  Factors for Retirement Income Credits earned between...
   when   Retirement

Vested Termination

If you have a vested Pension Benefit and terminate your employment with all Kaiser Permanente entities before
reaching age 65, you will be entitled to begin receiving the vested portion of your Pension Benefit as of the first
day of the month following your 65th birthday (provided you have notified the external administrator of your

                  KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 75
RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

intention to retire at least 60 days before your normal retirement date). To be eligible for a vested termination
Pension Benefit, you must have completed at least 3 years of vesting service.

To determine your benefit, multiply the amount of your benefit by your vested percentage:

Years of Vesting Service  Vested Percentage
      Less than 3 years
             3 years             0 percent
             4 years            50 percent
             5 years            60 percent
             6 years            70 percent
             7 years            80 percent
                                100 percent

Note: If you terminated employment with KFHPW before January 1, 1989 with only 7 years of vesting service
and did not accumulate additional vesting service following a rehire, you are only 90 percent vested in your Plan
benefit.

If your employment ends with all Kaiser Permanente entities and you are eligible to receive a vested benefit in the
future, it is your responsibility to keep Kaiser Permanente informed whenever your address changes, even though
you may not yet be receiving benefits. Important information about the Plan and your vested benefits may be
mailed to you from time to time. Failure to keep the external administrator informed of your current address (or
the name and current address of your beneficiary) could result in the delay of receipt of your benefits. It is your
responsibility to contact the external administrator at least 60 days before the date you wish to start your benefit
payments.

Early Retirement

Although benefits normally begin at age 65--the Plan's normal retirement age--you may decide to begin
receiving benefits as early as the first day of the month following your 55th birthday, provided your employment
with all Kaiser Permanente entities has terminated. You must contact the external administrator and submit an
application for benefits at least 60 days before the date you want retirement benefits to begin.

Retirement benefits that begin before normal retirement age are reduced to reflect the fact that payments start
sooner and are expected to be paid over a longer period of time. The amount of reduction depends on your age at
the time payments begin, as this chart shows:

Disability Retirement

If it is determined that you are disabled on the date you terminate employment with all Kaiser Permanente
entities, you terminate employment for reasons other than death, and when you terminate you are neither (1) at
least age 55 with at least 12 years of vesting service, nor (2) eligible for normal or late retirement, you may be
eligible for a disability retirement benefit following your termination of employment.

You will be considered "disabled" if you have been determined by the Social Security Administration to be eligible
for Social Security disability income benefits. Alternatively, you may also be considered disabled if Kaiser
Permanente has determined, based on competent medical evidence submitted by a physician, that you are
permanently disabled from performing the normal duties of your position because of your disability by bodily
injuries or disease.

However, if you had long term disability (LTD) insurance coverage through an Organization-sponsored benefit
plan as of the date of the termination of your employment, you will not be eligible for disability retirement
benefits until you have exhausted the benefits (if any) that are available under that LTD coverage or you reach age
55.

This means you must apply for any LTD benefits that you may be eligible for and, if you are approved for LTD
benefits, you must continue to receive the benefits until they are exhausted or you reach age 55. (You cannot
voluntarily end LTD benefits prior to that date. If you apply for LTD benefits and are denied, or if you do not
have LTD insurance coverage through a Kaiser Permanente-sponsored benefit plan as of the date of the
termination of your employment, then you will be eligible for disability retirement benefits provided that you
satisfy the other requirements described above.

If you qualify for a Disability Retirement benefit, you will be entitled to such benefit regardless of your age or
years of vesting service. For purposes of determining your disability retirement benefit, you will be 100 percent
vested in the retirement income credits you have earned to date. Note this accelerated vesting does not apply to
any vested termination benefit you may be entitled to if you recover from your disability before age 65.

Disability Retirement benefits are reduced to reflect the fact that payments may start sooner and, therefore, may
be paid over a longer period of time, using these reduction factors:

KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 77
RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

                 55 or younger                                      56.67 percent
                                                                    53.33 percent
                                                                    50.00 percent

Your Disability Retirement benefit will never be less than 50 percent of your total retirement income credits, even
if your monthly payments begin before age 55. After your Disability Retirement benefit starts, it will generally
continue for the rest of your life. However, if you recover from your disability before age 65, the monthly pension
will stop. If at the time you became disabled you were eligible for a vested termination benefit, your vested
termination benefit will begin when you reach age 65. (The monthly benefit amount will be reduced to take into
account the disability retirement benefits already received.)

How Benefits Are Paid

You must complete and return a retirement commencement package and any other required forms or
documentation to receive your earned plan benefit. To begin the commencement process, visit at kp.org/myhr,
click on the Benefits & Wellness tab, then click the Retirement link under Retirement Benefits, then click on
My Pension Plan under Defined Benefits Pension Plans.

When you apply for your benefit, you can select the standard form of payment or one of the alternate forms of
payment. It is important to consider the available forms of payment carefully before making your selection. Once
you begin to receive benefits, you cannot change your form of payment. The form of payment you select may have
a number of tax implications. You should carefully consider your personal financial situation when selecting a
form of payment. The plan, its fiduciaries and its sponsoring employers cannot offer financial or tax advice on this
subject. For assistance, please consult a tax advisor or financial planner.

Under the terms of the Plan, your election may not be made more than 180 days in advance of your benefit
commencement date, but must be made at least 30 days in advance of that date. However, you may waive the
30-day requirement with your spouse's consent. Generally, you should notify the Plan administrator of your desire
to begin receiving Plan benefits at least 60 days before the date you would like your monthly payments to start.

Standard Forms of Payment

If you are single: the standard form of payment is the Single Life Annuity.

If you are married: your spouse is entitled by federal law to receive benefits, so your standard form of payment is
the 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity. Therefore, you are legally required to obtain your spouse's consent to

KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 78
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

elect other forms of payment. The consent must be in writing and notarized no more than 90 days before the
benefits begin.

Please see below for descriptions of these and the other available forms of payment under the plan.

Available Forms of Payment

Ě Lump Sum: Under this option, you receive a one-time lump sum amount. After you receive the Lump Sum
  payment, there are no more payments due under the plan. The Lump Sum can be rolled over into a traditional
  IRA, Roth IRA or another employer's qualified plan, if that plan accepts rollovers.

Ě Single Life Annuity: Under this option, you receive a monthly pension benefit until your death. However, all
  pension payments stop when you die regardless of marital status. This is the standard form of payment if you
  are not married (as defined by federal law) on your Benefit Commencement Date.

Ě 50 percent, 75 percent, and 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuities: You must be married or in a
  domestic partnership to receive a joint and survivor annuity (JSA) payment form. With any of the Joint and
  Survivor Annuities, you receive a monthly benefit for as long as you live. If you die before your spouse/domestic
  partner, your spouse/domestic partner will receive the specified percentage (50 percent, 75 percent or 100
  percent) of the amount you received for the remainder of your spouse's/domestic partner's lifetime. If your
  spouse/domestic partner dies first, payments end upon your death. Because the Joint and Survivor Annuity
  payment options guarantee a pension over the lives of 2 people, the payment amount you receive each month is
  less than you would receive under the single life annuity form. The reduction depends on the type of Joint and
  Survivor Annuity you choose, and upon your age and your spouse's/domestic partner's age when your benefits
  begin. IRS regulations may limit the available Joint and Survivor Annuity options for domestic partners who are
  more than 10 years younger than the participant.If you are married at the time you receive your first pension
  payment, payment will be in the form of a 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity unless you choose a different
  form of payment. Any form of payment other than a 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity requires your
  spouse's written consent, witnessed by a Plan representative or notary public.

Ě 10-Year Guarantee: This payment option provides a monthly benefit to you for the rest of your life, with a
  guaranteed minimum total payment equal to 120 times the monthly single life annuity amount you could have
  elected. That means that when you die, the external administrator will add up all payments you received, and
  compare the total to the guaranteed minimum. If the amount you have received is less than the guaranteed
  minimum, your beneficiary will receive the balance in a lump sum. Note: The monthly benefit amount is less
  than the monthly amount you would have received under a single life annuity. However, the guaranteed
  minimum is based on the single life annuity amount (which is higher than the amount you were receiving each
  month). As a result, your beneficiary may receive a guaranteed payment even if you received more than 120
  payments (10 years of payments).

Ě Fixed Monthly Installments: With this option, you receive the actuarial lump sum present value of your entire
  Pension Benefit in a series of substantially equal annual (or more frequent) installments. The installment
  amount is adjusted to reflect the fact that benefits are paid over time in installments.

Ě Social Security Adjustment Option: This form of payment is a variation of the single life annuity option: it
  provides you with a monthly benefit for your lifetime with all payments stopping when you die, but allows you
  to coordinate your pension with your estimated Social Security benefits. Your pension benefit will be adjusted so
  that the sum of your monthly pension payment under the Plan and your monthly Social Security benefit is
  roughly equal before and after you reach Social Security age. This option allows you to smooth out, as much as
  possible, your monthly retirement income before and after Social Security age. Please note that if you choose

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 79
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

  this option, the actual total of your Pension Plan and Social Security benefits may not be the same each month,
  for one or more of the following reasons:
  Ě The Plan provides 2 versions of this option - one that assumes you begin receiving Social Security benefits at

     age 62, the other assuming that you begin receiving those benefits at age 65. You may select either option.
     However, the date that you actually start to receive Social Security benefits may be either of these dates, or
     another date altogether. A difference between the date you actually begin to receive Social Security benefits
     and the date assumed under the option you choose will result in variation in your monthly total retirement
     income from the Plan and Social Security.
  Ě Your actual Social Security benefit may vary from the estimate that is used in computing the monthly
     Pension Benefit under this option. In that event, your total monthly retirement income from this Plan and
     Social Security may not be the same before and after you reach Social Security age.
  Ě The monthly pension payment from the Plan under this form is reduced upon your attainment of the age
     elected (i.e., age 62 or 65), not the actual date you begin receiving Social Security benefits. However, due to
     administrative processes at the Social Security Administration, there may be a lag of a month or more
     between the date you attain a given age and the date you receive your first Social Security check (assuming
     that you timely applied to commence Social Security benefits upon reaching that age). In that event, there
     will be a temporary reduction in the total of the retirement income you receive from the Plan and Social
     Security.

The amount payable under each method is determined using actuarial assumptions and the interest rate specified
by the plan. You will be provided with estimates of the amounts payable under each of the different methods as
part of your commencement package.

Domestic Partners and Civil Union Partners

Although Kaiser Permanente recognizes domestic partnerships and civil unions, the federal government, which
regulates many of our benefit plans, does not. Thus, wherever the terms "married" and "spouse" are used in this
Summary Plan Description (SPD), they mean a couple that has entered into a legal marriage. Civil union partners
are eligible for the same benefits as domestic partners and are subject to the same restrictions that apply to
domestic partners. Therefore, all references in this SPD to domestic partners and domestic partnerships also apply
to civil union partners.
You may designate a domestic partner as joint annuitant under a Joint and Survivor Annuity if, before benefits
begin, either: (1) your partnership is state-registered, or (2) you have a valid affidavit of domestic partnership on
file with the Plan. To submit an affidavit, contact the Plan administrator. If you are in a domestic partnership at
the time your pension payments begin, payment will be in the form of a single life annuity unless you elect a
different form of payment. You may choose a different option if you prefer.

Required Distribution of Small Benefits

If at the time your employment ends:
Ě The value of your vested benefit is $1,000 or less, or
Ě The value of your vested benefit is $5,000 or less, and

     - You are age 65 or over, or

     - The benefit is payable to a beneficiary or alternate payee

your vested benefit will automatically be distributed to you (or your beneficiary or alternate payee) as a lump sum
cash distribution unless you (or your beneficiary or alternate payee) elect a different distribution option such as a

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 80
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

rollover within 60 days after being notified of the available payment options, or unless otherwise provided in a
qualified domestic relations order.

Optional Distribution of Small Benefits

If at the time you terminate employment your vested Pension Benefit payable in the form of a single life annuity
commencing at age 65 is less than $100 per month, you may elect to receive your pension in the form of an
immediate lump sum cash distribution.

The After-tax 2 Percent Account

This section about the After-tax 2 Percent Account applies to you if, before the applicable effective date, you made 2
percent contributions on an after-tax basis. If you are unsure if you have an After-tax 2 Percent Account, please contact
the Plan administrator.
In the past, staff members were required to contribute 2 percent of certified earnings to a retirement account as a
condition of participating in the Plan (and earning pension (DB) benefits).
If you participated in the Plan before November 2009, you may have made those 2 percent contributions on a
pretax basis to a separate retirement plan, then known as the Group Health Cooperative 2 Percent Retirement
Plan. In 2010, the 2 Percent Retirement Plan was merged into the Group Health Cooperative 403(b)(7) Custodial
Plan, and then in 2017, was renamed the Kaiser Permanente Washington 403(b) Plan. Active staff members are
currently allowed to make voluntary pretax salary deferral contributions to the Kaiser Permanente Washington
403(b) Plan.
Please see the Kaiser Permanente Washington 403(b) Plan section for more information about your rights with
respect to your account (if any) in that plan.
If you previously made after-tax 2 percent contributions, these contributions remain within the Plan in
an After-tax 2 Percent Account.

The requirement to make after-tax 2 percent contributions as a condition of participating in the Plan ceased as of
June 23, 2012.
After June 23, 2012, employees were no longer required (or allowed) to make contributions to the After-tax 2
Percent Account.
If, in the past, you made contributions to the After-tax 2 Percent Account:
Ě Your 2 percent contributions and any account earnings grow on a tax-deferred basis; this means you will be not

  taxed on any investment gains until you receive a distribution from your account (funds representing your
  after-tax contributions to your 2 Percent Account are not taxed upon distribution).
Ě You are always fully vested in your 2 Percent Account balance; if your employment with all Kaiser
  Permanente entities ends at any time or for any reason, you can either leave your funds in the account until you
  reach age 72 or receive an immediate distribution of your funds.
If you previously made pretax 2 percent contributions to the 2 Percent Retirement Plan, see the Kaiser
Permanente Washington 403(b) Plan section for more information. If all of your 2 percent contributions were
made on a pretax basis, you do not have an After-tax 2 Percent Account in this Plan.

Vesting

Vesting is ownership of your After-tax 2 Percent Account balance. You are always 100 percent vested in the
current value of your own contributions to the After-tax 2 Percent Account (as adjusted for investment gains and
losses).

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 81
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Investment of Your After-tax 2 Percent Account Balance

Making your contribution after-tax means the income you use to make your contribution is taxed in the same year
in which you contribute it. When you withdraw your after-tax contributions, you will not be taxed again on the
amounts you contributed but you will be taxed on any investment earnings and net gains on those contributions.
Your money goes into an investment fund with the Plan's trustee. Currently the fund used for the After-tax 2
Percent Account is a balanced fund designed for saving for retirement that adjusts it underlying asset mix over
time (often called a target date fund). The balanced fund seeks to provide a reasonable rate of return by investing
in a diversified portfolio of stocks and bonds.
For more information on this investment fund, call the Plan administrator or visit the Plan's website at
www.journeytoretirement.com.

When You Can Receive Your Account Balance

You may not make any withdrawals or take any loans from the Plan (including the After-tax 2 Percent Account)
while you are employed with Kaiser Permanente. Once your employment with all Kaiser Permanente entities ends
for any reason, you can withdraw from your After-tax 2 Percent Account at any time, subject to normal tax rules
and penalties. See Tax Considerations for tax information.
If your employment with all Kaiser Permanente entities KFHPW ends, you may leave your account balance in the
Plan up to age 72. You must begin receiving a distribution from your account by April 1 of the year following the
year you reach age 72 or terminate employment with KFHPW, whichever is later.

After-tax 2 Percent Account Maintenance Fee

If you have an After-tax 2 Percent Account, when your employment with all Kaiser Permanente entities ends, your
account will be assessed a quarterly account maintenance fee. The fee is deducted the last week of each quarter,
starting with the quarter following your termination of employment. For example, if your employment ends on
March 30, you would be assessed the fee the week ending June 30. As of July 2017, the account maintenance fee
was $27.48 per year ($6.87 per quarter). The amount of the fee may change from time to time.

Your Benefit Payment Options

Generally, benefits from your After-tax 2 Percent Account will be paid in a single lump-sum cash payment as soon
as administratively possible after your request for distribution. Alternatively, you may choose from a variety of
payment options, including:
Ě Direct rollover (your account balance may be directly rolled over into a traditional or Roth IRA or your new

  employer's eligible retirement plan)
Ě Single lump sum
Ě Installments
Ě An annuity contract.
You may request information about these options from the Plan administrator at any time.
The Plan requires that your After-tax 2 Percent Account be paid in the form of an annuity unless you specifically
request otherwise.

Definition of Marriage

For the purpose of this Plan, your spouse is the person to whom you are legally married. If at the time you choose
to start benefits from your account, you are:

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 82
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Ě Not married, you will receive the single life annuity form of payment, unless you elect another form of
  payment. With a single life annuity, you receive a monthly benefit for your lifetime and payments stop at your
  death.

Ě Married, you will receive payment in the form of a 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity, unless you elect
  another form of payment. With the 100 percent Joint and Survivor Annuity, you receive a monthly benefit for
  as long as you live. If you die before your spouse/domestic partner, your spouse/domestic partner will receive the
  specified percentage (100 percent) of the amount you received for the remainder of your spouse's/domestic
  partner's lifetime. If your spouse/domestic partner dies first, payments end upon your death. IRS regulations
  may limit the available Joint and Survivor Annuity options for domestic partners who are more than 10 years
  younger than the participant.

You may choose a different payment option, but by law your spouse must provide his or her written consent
(witnessed by a Plan representative or notary public) to any other form of payment. Your spouse must also consent
to any election to name a different beneficiary.

Tax Considerations

After-tax 2 Percent Account

Distributions from your After-tax 2 Percent Account of amounts representing your contributions to the account
(after-tax contributions) are not taxable, but you will be taxed on any investment gains on those contributions.

Pension Benefit

Benefit distributions from this Plan are taxable income and should be reported on your federal income tax form.
Generally you may elect the amount of income tax withholding for distributions not eligible for rollover, but all
payments that are eligible rollover distributions are automatically subject to a 20 percent withholding tax if not
directly rolled over. The IRS requires that 20 percent of the taxable portion of your distribution be withheld for
prepayment of federal income tax. The actual taxes you owe at year-end will depend on your situation. The IRS
requires that 10 percent be withheld for prepayment of federal income tax for distributions that are not rollover
eligible if a tax election is not returned.

Rollovers

Distributions that are not eligible for rollover include:
Ě Lifetime annuity options offered by this Plan
Ě A series of substantially equal payments over your life or life expectancy (or the life or life expectancy of you and

  your beneficiary) or over a period of 10 or more years
Ě Lump sum distributions made to non-spouse beneficiaries (except for a direct rollover to an individual

  retirement account or individual retirement annuity)
Ě Plan payments that add up to less than $200 for an entire year
Ě Required minimum distributions (which must begin no later than April 1 following the year in which you reach

  age 72 or termination of employment, whichever is earlier).

At the time your benefit becomes eligible for a distribution, you have the choice of how the benefit will be
distributed. If your distribution is a lump sum payment, you must decide whether to make a direct rollover to an
IRA or another eligible retirement plan, or to receive the payment in cash.
By electing a direct rollover, you avoid the 20 percent withholding tax on the amount transferred. The plan
receiving the direct transfer can be any of the following, if they agree to accept a rollover:

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 83
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Ě Individual Retirement Arrangement (IRA)
Ě Roth IRA (if Roth IRA conversion rules are satisfied)
Ě Individual retirement annuity
Ě Annuity plan
Ě 401(a) qualified trust
Ě 403(b) annuity
Ě Eligible 457(b) plan, or
Ě Another employer's eligible retirement plan.
If you do not elect a direct rollover and instead take the distribution in a lump sum, you receive 80 percent of the
taxable amount in cash and the remaining 20 percent of the taxable amount will be withheld for federal income
tax. You will have 60 days from the date you receive the check to change your mind and roll over part or all of the
distribution, including the amount that was withheld for taxes. However, to roll over the entire amount including
the 20 percent withheld, you will have to supply the money to cover the amount withheld. The amount withheld
will be an advance payment to the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) of the federal income taxes that may be owed
for the year of the distribution.
In addition, any eligible distribution not rolled over is subject to a 10 percent early distribution penalty tax unless:
Ě You are age 55 or older at the time your employment with all Kaiser Permanente entities ends
Ě You are age 59Ż or older at the time of distribution
Ě The distribution was due to death or total and permanent disability
Ě The money was distributed under a Qualified Domestic Relations Order, or
Ě You have deductible medical expenses that exceed your retirement payments.
If you were born before January 1, 1936 and you have been in the Plan for at least 5 years or if you were a
participant in the Plan before 1974, you may qualify for special tax treatment on lump sum distributions. Please
consult your tax advisor for more information.

Tax Advice

You should consult a qualified tax advisor before making a benefit distribution election. There is no guarantee that
the tax treatment of benefits will not be altered by future changes in the law or regulations. State tax rules may
also apply. Only a qualified tax advisor can give advice on how the current tax regulations affect your specific
situation.

Additional Information

If You Take a Leave of Absence

If you take an approved leave of absence, you will continue to earn your normal hours of service for eligibility and
vesting toward your Pension Benefit, as long as you return to work when your leave expires. However, paid hours
associated solely with workers compensation, unemployment compensation or disability insurance laws will not be
included as hours counted towards meeting the minimum of 500 hours of service you must earn in order to earn a
"retirement income credit" for a plan year.

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 84
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

If You Serve in Uniformed Services

Under the Uniformed Services Employment and Reemployment Rights Act of 1994 (USERRA), you have certain
rights if you voluntarily or involuntarily leave employment to serve in any of the United States uniformed military
services (including the Coast Guard) for active duty or for training. To qualify for these rights, you must meet
both of the following requirements:
Ě You must give Human Resources advance written or verbal notice of your upcoming leave for military service,

  and

Ě You must report back to work within the time periods specified under USERRA, which vary depending on the
  length of your military service. Note, there are exceptions if you cannot return to work due to death or disability
  while performing qualified military service.

If you meet these requirements, then following your return to work, you will be eligible to receive the vesting
service and credited service you would have earned toward your Pension Benefit had you remained employed with
KFHPW.

For more information about reemployment rights for veterans, contact Human Resources.

If You Become Disabled

If it is determined that you are disabled on the date you terminate employment with any Kaiser Permanente
entity, you terminate employment for reasons other than death, and when you terminate you are neither (1) at
least age 55 with at least 12 years of vesting service, nor (2) eligible for normal or late retirement, you will be
eligible for a disability retirement benefit following your termination of employment.

However, if you had long term disability (LTD) insurance coverage through a Kaiser Permanente sponsored
benefit plan as of the date of the termination of your employment, you will not be eligible for disability retirement
benefits until you have exhausted the benefits (if any) that are available under that LTD coverage or you reach age
55.

You will be considered "disabled" if you have been determined by the Social Security Administration to be eligible
for Social Security disability income benefits. Alternatively, you will also be considered disabled if Kaiser
Permanente has determined based on competent medical evidence submitted by a physician that you are
permanently disabled from performing the normal duties of your position because of your disability by bodily
injuries or disease.

If you qualify for a Disability Retirement benefit, you will be entitled to a pension benefit from the Plan regardless
of your age or years of vesting service. For purposes of determining your disability retirement benefit, you will be
100 percent vested in the retirement income credits you have earned to date. (See Disability Termination).

You may receive your After-tax 2 Percent Account balance (if you have one) immediately following the date your
employment ends due to the disability in any of the optional payment forms offered by the Plan

If You Die

Before You Retire

If you die before you begin to receive benefit payments under the Plan, your beneficiary will be entitled to the
value of your After-tax 2 Percent Account balance (if you have one), as well as a death benefit based on the present
value of your vested Pension Benefit retirement income credits earned as of the date of your death. If you are
employed by Kaiser Permanente when you die, your retirement income credits will be fully vested as of the date of
death. If you die while performing qualified military service, your beneficiary will be entitled to benefits as if you
had resumed participation in the Plan and then ended employment with Kaiser Permanente due to your death.

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 85
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

The timing and the payment form for death benefits depends on whether your beneficiary is your spouse or
someone other than your spouse:
Ě Spouse beneficiaries. If you are married when you die, your spouse is your beneficiary, unless (with your

  spouse's written consent) you have named another person as beneficiary. The form of the death benefit for the
  Pension Benefit or the After-tax 2 Percent Account for a surviving spouse is a single life annuity, unless your
  spouse elects another form of payment. The benefit amount is calculated based on the vested portion of your
  benefit that would have commenced when you reached age 65 (or on the date of your death, if later). The
  benefit is payable as of the first of the month following the date of your death or at a later date chosen by your
  spouse, but not later than the date you would have reached age 72. A surviving spouse may roll over certain
  distributions from the Plan to an IRA or another employer's eligible plan. See Tax Considerations for more
  information. The amount of the spouse's benefit depends in part on whether the participant died before or after
  becoming eligible for retirement.
Ě Non-spouse beneficiaries. The form of death benefit for non-spouse beneficiaries (including domestic
  partners) is a single lump sum, unless the non-spouse beneficiary chooses another form of payment. The benefit
  amount is calculated based on the vested portion of your benefit that would have commenced when you
  reached age 65 (or on the date of your death, if later). The benefit is payable in a lump sum at any time within 5
  years following the date of your death, or in installments or an annuity commencing within one year following
  the date of your death. Death benefits received by non-spouse beneficiaries may be eligible for rollover. See Tax
  Considerations.
For recognition of a domestic partner under the Plan, you must have done one of the following before your death:
(1) your partnership must be state-registered, or (2) you must have a valid affidavit of domestic partnership on file
with the Plan. To submit an affidavit, contact the Plan administrator.

After You Retire

If you die after your Plan benefit payments have begun, death benefits for your spouse/domestic partner (or other
beneficiary) are determined by the benefit payment form that you elected when you retired. For instance, if you
chose the 100 percent joint and survivor annuity payment form and your spouse/domestic partner survives you,
your spouse/domestic partner will receive 100 percent of the monthly amount you were receiving, payable for his
or her lifetime. If you chose the single life annuity, however, benefits will stop upon your death.

Kaiser Permanente Washington Defined Contribution Plan

The Kaiser Permanente Washington Defined Contribution Plan (DC Plan), a qualified defined contribution
retirement savings plan, is a money purchase pension plan.

Who Is Eligible

If you are an employee of Kaiser Foundation Health Plan of Washington or Kaiser Foundation Health Plan of
Washington Options, Inc., in an eligible employment status, you may participate in the plan, regardless of your
work schedule, with the following exceptions:

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 86

Ě You are eligible to participate in the Kaiser Permanente Washington Defined Benefit Plan
Ě You are a leased employee
Ě You are a nonresident alien or perform your services outside the United States.
Ě You are a represented by a union subject to a collective bargaining agreement that does not provide for their

  participation in the plan
Ě You are a medical resident
If you are a temporary employee, you are eligible for the plan if you are classified as temporary and are:
Ě not covered by a collective bargaining agreement, or
Ě covered by a collective bargaining agreement that does not exclude them from participation in the plan, or
Ě considered to be in an eligible employee classification beginning on the six-month anniversary of your date of

  hire with Kaiser Permanente

When You Are Eligible

If you are a regular full-time or part-time employee, you are eligible to participate in the plan on your date of hire.
If you are a temporary employee, you may be eligible after six months from date of hire.
If you transitioned from Maui Regional Health System (MRHS) to Maui Health System (MHS) on July 1, 2017,
your prior service with MRHS will count toward the Years of Service eligibility requirements for this plan, as
applicable. You will need to provide sufficient evidence if you believe that your previous MRHS service is greater
than what Kaiser Permanente shows.

How to Enroll

When you are eligible for the plan, Kaiser Permanente automatically sets up an account for you and Vanguard

simple steps:
