Ě Click Beneficiaries under "Do It Yourself"

Making Contributions to Your Account

Pre-Tax Employee Contributions

Based on your election, contributions are deducted from your paycheck each pay period, and your gross pay will
be reduced by the amount of your contributions. Your contributions are deducted from your pay before federal
and state taxes are withheld. As a result, your taxable income -- the amount on which you pay taxes -- is reduced,
saving you tax dollars. Your actual tax savings will depend on your income level, exemptions, marital status,
deductions, and the current tax rates.

You can contribute between 1 percent and 75 percent of your eligible compensation each period, in whole
percentage increments. However, the maximum amount you can contribute to your plan account each year
cannot exceed the maximum contribution dollar limit allowed by the Internal Revenue Code (IRC) -- which is
$19,500 in 2021.

Unless you elect otherwise, your contribution rate will continue from year to year or until you reach a legal limit.

Your total contributions will be monitored on an ongoing basis and reviewed at the end of the year. If you exceed
your total contribution limit, you will be notified and refunded any excess contributions. For the most up-to-date
IRS limits, visit irs.gov and search for "contribution limits."

If You Are Age 50 or Older

If you are age 50 or older, or if you will reach age 50 by December 31 of a given year, you are eligible to make an
additional pre-tax catch-up contribution to your plan for that year and in subsequent years. The maximum
allowable catch-up contribution in 2021 is $6,500. Your annual contribution limit and catch-up contribution
limit may change from year to year.

You are eligible to make catch-up contributions only after you have reached your applicable annual contribution
limit. The following chart outlines the annual contribution limit in 2021:

Pre-Tax Contribution Limit Catch-Up Contribution Limit  Combined Contribution
                                                                     Limit

$19,500                     $6,500                               $26,000

If you wish to make catch-up contributions, you should review your current deferral rate to determine if you need
to increase it to take advantage of the combined contribution limit.

If you have any questions about the catch-up contributions, contact Vanguard, our third-party administrator, at
800-523-1188. For the most up-to-date IRS limits, visit irs.gov and search for "contribution limits."

         KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 95
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Rollover Contributions

You may consolidate your retirement savings by rolling over pre-tax or after-tax contributions from qualifying
IRAs and vested balances from 403(b) or 401(k) plans that you have with previous employers into your plan
account. You must complete a rollover contribution form and submit it to Vanguard. More information is
available online at www.vanguard.com or by calling Vanguard's VOICE network at 800-523-1188.

Transfer Contributions

If you have a 401(k) account related to your employment with KPWA Options, you are able to transfer the
balance of that account into the plan. This type of contribution is called a transfer contribution. To make a
transfer contribution, you must complete an asset transfer form and submit it to Vanguard.

Employer Contributions

If eligible, on your date of hire, your employer will begin to make contributions to your account.
Kaiser Permanente will provide a 100 percent match on up to 2.7 percent of your eligible earnings per pay period.
However, to receive the full 2.7 percent match, your employee contribution must be at least 3 percent of your
eligible earnings. The Social Security wage base for calendar year 2021 is $142,800.

Eligibility for Employer Matching Contributions

You are an eligible staff member for purposes of employer matching contributions and eligible to receive matching
contributions unless you are:
Ě a leased employee
Ě an independent contractor
Ě a nonresident alien
Ě an employee classified by KFHPW as a temporary employee (except as provided below)
Ě a medical resident
Ě covered by a collective bargaining agreement that does not require employer matching contributions to the Plan
on your behalf.
Please note: a KFHPW staff member classified as temporary will become eligible to receive matching
contributions on the six-month anniversary of his or her first day of employment, unless he or she is covered by a
collective bargaining agreement that excludes temporary staff from eligibility for matching contributions.

Optimization Feature
If your contributions to the plan stop during the year -- for example, because you reach the pre-tax maximum
contribution limit before the end of the year -- your matching contributions will be optimized as long as
Ě you are employed on December 31 of that year or
Ě your termination of employment during the year was due to your death or disability or
Ě your termination occurred after you reached age 65)
Here's how it works:
At the end of each year, Kaiser Permanente will calculate the 50 percent matching contribution on the amount
you contributed to the plan -- up to 4 percent of eligible earnings. If the actual matching contribution is less than

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 96
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

the calculated amount, Kaiser Permanente will make an additional matching contribution after the end of the
year, to ensure that you receive the full matching contribution you are entitled to.
For example, Carolyn decides to contribute at a rate of 10 percent, but has to stop contributing mid-year for
personal reasons. She makes $50,000 a year, paid over 26 pay periods.
For each pay period, she earns $1,923 and contributes 10 percent of that, or $192 dollars, into her retirement
savings plan. She stops after 13 pay periods and contributes $2,500 in total for the year. Kaiser Permanente's
matching contributions up to that point total about $500 (2 percent of $1,923, X 13 pay periods = $500).
If Carolyn had contributed throughout the entire year, Kaiser Permanente's match would have been $1,000 or 2
percent of $50,000.
Therefore, because Carolyn contributed 5 percent of her annual pay to the plan when you consider the whole year
($2,500/$50,000), Kaiser Permanente will contribute, through the optimization feature, another $500 (the
difference between $500 and $1,000) to the retirement savings plan after the end of the year, to ensure she gets the
full 2 percent employer match for the year.

Maximum Compensation Limit

The maximum compensation limit is the annual eligible pay under the Internal Revenue Code (IRC) that may be
considered for benefit purposes. The maximum compensation limit for 2021 is $290,000. This amount may be
indexed periodically for cost-of-living increases. Employer contributions to your account will only be calculated on
pay up to the maximum compensation limit. In addition, your annual maximum contribution may be limited by
the IRC. For the most up-to-date IRS limits, visit irs.gov and search for "contribution limits."

Annual Addition Limit

The maximum amount you and your employer can contribute cannot exceed the annual addition limit which is
the least of the following:
Ě The maximum limit allowed by the Internal Revenue Code (IRC) -- which is $58,000 in 2021
Ě 100 percent of your annual compensation
Annual addition limits are calculated and monitored throughout the year. Your employee and employer
contributions automatically stop when you reach your contribution limit. If you reach the limit, Vanguard will
automatically restart your contribution the first pay period of the following year. For the most up-to-date IRS
limits, visit irs.gov and search for "contribution limits."

Non-Discrimination Test

The benefits you may receive from the defined contribution plan may be subject to a federally required
discrimination test. This complex test compares the benefits of the "highly compensated" to the benefits of the
"non-highly compensated" participants under all applicable plans provided by Kaiser Permanente and may require
a reduction in benefits for the "highly compensated" participants.
Because of this test, if you are highly compensated (as defined by statute), the amount of your contributions may
be reduced below the annual maximums to comply with the rules. You will be notified during the year if this
reduction applies to you.

Vesting

Vesting refers to your entitlement to a benefit. Once you are vested, you are entitled to a distribution of your
account when you leave Kaiser Permanente.

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 97
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Employee Contributions
You are immediately 100 percent vested in your pre-tax employee contributions to your plan account. This means
that you are entitled to the total value of your contributions and any investment earnings in your account when
you leave Kaiser Permanente.

Employer Contributions
You are fully vested in the employer contribution account portion of the plan.

Choosing Your Beneficiary

When you become a participant, you should name a beneficiary to receive payment of your account if you die.
You may choose anyone you want as your beneficiary, However, if you are married and you want to choose
someone other than your spouse as your beneficiary, your beneficiary designation must be accompanied by a
written, notarized statement of your spouse's consent to be valid. You may change your designated beneficiary at
any time, except as described for your spouse.
Please see the If You Die section for more information.

Domestic Partners and Civil Union Partners

Although Kaiser Permanente recognizes domestic partnerships and civil unions, the federal government, which
regulates many of our benefit plans, does not. Thus, wherever the terms "married" and "spouse" are used in this
SPD, they mean a couple that has entered into a legal marriage. Civil union partners are eligible for the same
benefits as domestic partners and are subject to the same restrictions that apply to domestic partners. Therefore, all
references in this SPD to domestic partners and domestic partnerships also apply to civil union partners.

Choosing Your Investments

You can invest your account among a diversified lineup of investment options. In addition, you are eligible to
invest your account through the Vanguard Brokerage Option. You can invest up to 50 percent of your fully vested
account in the Vanguard Brokerage Option. Investment funds are reviewed by the Investment Committee on an
ongoing basis, and the actual funds offered through the plan are subject to change. A complete list of funds and
more information about the Vanguard Brokerage Option is available online at www.vanguard.com or by calling
Vanguard's VOICE network at 800-523-1188. You may also obtain information and make changes to your
account on your mobile device. Go to vanguard.com/bemobile to download the Vanguard app so you can
access your account on the go.
Upon becoming a participant, any contributions to your account will be invested in the Qualified Default
Investment Alternative (QDIA) until you select an investment option. The QDIA is the KP Retirement Path
Fund with the target date closest to the year in which you will reach age 65. The KP Retirement Path Funds are
invested in several broadly diversified funds and are subject to the risks of their underlying funds. The year in the
fund name refers to the approximate year (the target date) when an investor in the fund would attain age 65. The
fund will gradually shift its emphasis from more aggressive investments to more conservative ones based on its
target date. Contact Vanguard to learn about your QDIA fund.
The plan is intended to satisfy the requirements of Section 404(c) of the Employee Retirement Income Security
Act (ERISA) and Department of Labor Regulation Section 2550.404c-1. In general, this means that you are solely
responsible for any investment losses caused by your investment decisions. Kaiser Permanente, its directors,
officers, employees, subsidiaries, plan fiduciaries, and the trustee do not guarantee or insure the performance of
any of the investment funds offered by the plan, and will not be liable for those losses.

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 98
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Since you alone will be responsible for the losses or gains that result from your investment decisions, it is very
important that you carefully consider the investment options available to you.
You should note that in the event that a proxy voting decision is required regarding shares of the investment
funds, the investment fund shares will be voted on by the fiduciary for the plan in accordance with the investment
guidelines for the plan.
The plan administrator is the plan fiduciary responsible for providing participants and beneficiaries with the
information necessary for making informed decisions under the plan. To request additional information from the
plan administrator, please see the contact information provided in this Summary Plan Description. In addition, the
Plan provides a variety of tools and services available to help you make your investment decisions, like the
Vanguard Managed Account Program (VMAP) and Personal Online Advisor.

Changing Your Investments

You can change the investment of your account on Vanguard's website, by calling Vanguard's VOICE network,
or on your mobile device using the Vanguard app. You can redirect all future contributions to new investment
options (a contribution allocation change) as well as reinvest your balance -- including your past contributions --
among options (an exchange).

Receiving Information About Your Investments

You may obtain information and make changes to your account by signing on to Vanguard's website, by calling
Vanguard's VOICE network, or on your mobile device using the Vanguard app. You may monitor the activity in
your plan accounts as well as initiate transactions. You may also obtain your account balance, confirm your
investment allocations for future contributions, or request a transaction. Updated information about account
transactions is available at approximately 8 a.m. Eastern time on the day after the transaction is processed.

Borrowing From Your Account

If you have at least $2,000 in your plan account as of your loan application date, you can borrow up to 50 percent
of your vested account balance or $50,000, whichever is less, in any 12-month period. At no time can you borrow
more than $50,000 from your combined defined contribution plans, if you participate in more than one plan. The
minimum loan amount is $1,000. Only one loan per plan is permitted at a time.
You pay the principal and interest back to your own account through regular payroll deductions. The interest rate
applied to loans is the prime rate quoted by Reuters on the first business day of the month, plus 2 percent.
As described below, you can borrow on a short-term or long-term basis:
Ě If you borrow on a short-term basis, you must repay the loan within 12 to 60 months from the loan issue date.
Ě If you borrow on a long-term basis, you must repay the loan within 61 to 180 months. Long-term loans are

  available only when you are purchasing your primary residence.
There is a $50 loan application fee applied to each loan.
Your loan repayments are made on an after-tax basis. You must repay the entire loan before you can borrow from
your account again .
Your loan is not subject to taxes or penalties unless the loan defaults. A loan defaults if it is not repaid on a timely
basis or if it is not repaid in full when your employment ends.
You can find out how much you can borrow from your plan account or calculate different loan repayment
amounts and schedules by logging on to www.vanguard.com or by calling VOICE to speak to a Vanguard
Participant Services associate.

                                       KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 99
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

If you are married, federal law requires that your spouse consent to all loans. As a result, your application for a
loan must be accompanied by a written, notarized statement of your spouse's consent.

If You Go on an Unpaid Leave of Absence

If you go on an unpaid leave of absence, payroll deductions for your plan loan automatically stop. You have the
option to make manual payments directly to Vanguard, or to suspend your loan payments for up to 12 months or
when you return from your leave, whichever is earlier. However, the loan period does not increase, so you must
make up any missed payments by the original due date for the loan.
When you return from an unpaid leave of absence your loan payments will automatically restart. Once you return
to work, you will have the option to either pay all missed payments in a lump sum, or you may reamortize the
loan. If you decide to reamortize the loan, your loan payments are recalculated at a higher payroll deduction
amount so that the loan is paid by the end of the original agreed term of the loan.
If you are on an unpaid leave of absence for more than 12 months, and you do not arrange to make up missed
payments on a manual basis, the balance owing on your loan is deemed to be distributed to you. The distribution
is considered taxable income in the year you receive it, and you may also be subject to tax penalties, depending on
your age and employment status. Special rules apply if you are on a military leave of absence.

If You Transfer to Another Employee Group or Terminate Employment

If you transfer to another employee group or terminate employment before your loan is repaid, please contact
Vanguard in advance (if possible) to determine how this will affect your loan.

When You Can Receive a Distribution

Normally, you are entitled to receive your plan account balance when your employment with Kaiser Permanente
ends. You can defer receiving payment until April 1 of the year following your termination or the year you reach
72, whichever is later, if you have more than $5,000 in your account.
When Vanguard receives notice of your termination date, you will receive account distribution information and
forms. You will receive payment as soon as administratively possible, once Vanguard receives your forms.
If you plan to re-invest your distribution or roll over your distribution into another employer's qualified plan or an
IRA, you should compare the investment options and plan administrative and investment fees for both your
current plan as well as the new plan or IRA to determine your best financial option.
You may not take a distribution while employed by Kaiser Permanente, except as noted below. Thus, if you
terminate from one Kaiser Permanente Entity and transfer to or are re-employed by another Kaiser Permanente
Entity, you may not take a distribution from this plan during your employment with your new Entity.

In-Service Withdrawal

Age 59Ż Withdrawal
If you are at least 59Ż and still employed at Kaiser Permanente, you can withdraw your pre-tax employee
contributions, rollover contributions, and applicable investment earnings from your plan account.

Hardship Withdrawal
Based on federal requirements, while you are employed at Kaiser Permanente, you can withdraw pre-tax employee
contributions from the plan before you reach age 59Ż only in case of financial hardship. Investment earnings,
employer contributions, and rollover contributions from another retirement plan are not eligible to be withdrawn
for financial hardship.

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 100
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Financial hardship includes money needed for the following:
Ě College tuition for yourself, your spouse or domestic partner, or your dependents
Ě Medical expenses for yourself, your spouse or domestic partner, or your dependents
Ě Purchasing your primary residence or avoiding eviction from or foreclosure on your home
Ě Certain expenses relating to the repair of damage to your principal residence that qualifies as a casualty

  deduction
Ě Payments for burial or funeral expenses for your deceased parent, spouse, domestic partner, or dependent
Ě Money needed for specified expenses and losses you incur on account of a disaster declared by the Federal

  Emergency Management Agency (FEMA)

For a complete list of hardship circumstances, contact Vanguard at 800-523-1188.
Please note: Domestic partners and dependents must satisfy the requirements of the plan before a distribution
can be taken on their behalf.
To qualify for a financial hardship withdrawal, you must be able to confirm that you cannot obtain the money
you need from any other source (excluding any loans from your retirement account).
You must complete a hardship withdrawal application. If your application is approved, you will receive your
withdrawal as soon as administratively possible. It is taxable as ordinary income, and you may also owe federal and
state tax penalties for early withdrawal.
If you are married, federal law requires that your spouse consent to all withdrawals. As a result, your application
for a withdrawal must be accompanied by a written, notarized consent from your spouse.

Disability Withdrawal
In addition, you may receive a distribution from your vested account due to a disability, as defined under the plan,
while you are employed. Generally, this requires that you are totally disabled.

How Benefits Are Paid

When you terminate or retire from Kaiser Permanente with a defined contribution account balance of $5,000 or
less, your account will be closed at the end of the quarter following the quarter in which you terminate, and the
balance rolled into an individual retirement account in your name. However, before your account is closed, you
have the option to request a full distribution of the remaining balance.
You can elect to receive a distribution of your full account balance, or, if the value of your account is more than
$5,000, you can elect to receive a portion of your account and designate the specific type of contributions within
your account to be distributed. If you elect a partial distribution and your account is invested in multiple
investments, your distribution will be withdrawn proportionally from all of your investments.
Please note: If you request a partial distribution, you must continue to maintain an account balance greater than
$5,000 when you retire or terminate your employment with Kaiser Permanente for your account to remain open.
If the value of your account is more than $5,000, you can select any of the following available forms of payment:
Ě Lump Sum: Payment in a single sum of all or a portion of your vested account.
Ě Installments: The value of your account is paid to you in monthly, quarterly, or annual installments over a

  period of two to 25 years. In no event shall the payment extend beyond your life expectancy, nor shall any
  payment, except the last, be less than $100. You continue to direct the investment of your account until the

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 101
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

  installment payments are completed. You may request a total or partial distribution of your remaining account
  at any time.
  Your installment options include declining balance, fixed dollar, or fixed percentage payments. Declining
  balance payments allow you to take regular installments over a specific number of years, based on the remaining
  number of payments and your balance at the time of each payment. Fixed dollar payments allow you to specify
  the dollar amounts you would like to withdraw at intervals you choose (monthly, quarterly, annually). Fixed
  percentage payments allow you to specify the percentage of your balance you would like to withdraw at intervals
  you choose (monthly, quarterly, annually).

Required Distribution of Small Accounts

If, following the termination of your employment with Kaiser Permanente, the value of your account is $5,000 or
less and you do not request distribution of your benefits, your benefit will be rolled over into an Individual
Retirement Account (IRA) in your name. This automatic distribution may take place as early as the end of the
first quarter following your termination of employment with Kaiser Permanente. Vanguard will contact you if this
applies to you. Once the IRA is established, you will receive additional information. If you participate in more
than one defined contribution plan, your plan balances will not be aggregated for purposes of the $5,000
threshold.

Military Personnel Distributions

If you are in active duty military service for at least 30 days, you can elect to receive a distribution of your pre-tax
contributions (as adjusted for investment gains or losses). If you receive such a distribution, your right to make
contributions to the plan will be suspended for six months after the date of the distribution.
If you were ordered or called to active duty for at least 180 days or for an indefinite period as provided in Section
72(t)(2)(G) of the Internal Revenue Code, you can make a penalty-free withdrawal from your plan account while
on active duty. If you make such a withdrawal, you may, at any time within the two-year period beginning on the
day after the end of your active duty period, make one or more contributions to an individual retirement account
in an aggregate amount not exceeding the amount of your penalty-free withdrawal(s) from the plan.

If You Die

Here is what happens if you die before you commence your vested benefits from the plan or if you have a vested
benefit remaining in your account:
Ě If you have a valid beneficiary designation on file, payment will be made to your beneficiary (or beneficiaries).
Ě If you do not have a valid designated beneficiary on file at the time of your death or if your designated

  beneficiary dies and you have not named another beneficiary before your death, payment of your account will
  be made in the following order:

     - To your surviving legal spouse
     - If none, to your surviving children (natural or adopted) on an equal share basis
     - If none, to your surviving parents on an equal share basis
     - If none, then to your estate
If the remaining balance is more than $5,000, your beneficiary may elect any form of payment and may defer
receiving payment until April 1 of the year following the year in which you would have reached age 72. Your
beneficiary may elect a tax-free rollover to an IRA.
If you die while performing qualified military service, your survivors will receive any additional benefits (other

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 102
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

than benefit accruals for the period of your military service) that would have been provided under the plan had
you died immediately after returning from military service and resuming participation in the plan.

Tax Considerations

Your plan has been designed to provide you with significant tax advantages as long as your contributions remain in
your account. When you receive your account balance, however, it will be considered taxable income for the year
in which you receive it. In some cases, favorable tax treatment may be available.
The federal government also requires that 20 percent of the taxable portion of most distributions be automatically
withheld unless you directly transfer your distribution to a tax-deferred Individual Retirement Account (IRA), to
another Kaiser Permanente-sponsored defined contribution plan, or another employer's qualified plan.

If you are under age 55 when you terminate and you receive a distribution before age 59Ż, the taxable portion
may be subject to significant tax penalties, unless you roll your distribution over to an IRA or another qualified
plan.
If you turn age 55 or older in the year you terminate, any subsequent distribution you take in that year or later is
exempt from the penalty tax.
Benefit payments that are part of a series of payments over a lifetime are not eligible to be rolled over. Because the
tax laws regarding plan distributions are complicated, you may want to consult a tax advisor before you choose a
distribution from the plan.

Rollovers to Another Plan or Tax-Deferred IRA

Taxable distributions from your plan may be rolled over into another employer's qualified plan or a tax-deferred
IRA. If an eligible distribution is rolled over, income taxes will be deferred until you later withdraw the funds.
Remember that you may leave your account in your current plan until you are required to take a minimum
distribution (see "Minimum Distribution Requirement"). Before choosing to roll over your distributions into
another employer's qualified plan or an IRA, you should compare the investment options and plan administrative
and investment fees for both your current plan as well as the new plan or IRA to determine your best financial
option.
Please note: Hardship withdrawals may not be rolled over to another employer's qualified plan or to an IRA.

Non-Spouse Beneficiary Rollovers

Non-spouse beneficiaries, such as domestic partners, children, parents and siblings may elect to roll over eligible
survivor benefit distributions from the plan to an "inherited" IRA that is set up specifically to receive such
contributions.

Rollovers to a Roth IRA

You, your spouse, and non-spouse beneficiaries may roll over qualified amounts of plan distributions directly into
a Roth IRA. Income taxes on the taxable portion of your distribution will not be deferred if you elect to roll over
to a Roth IRA. Because tax laws regarding rollovers to a Roth IRA are complex, you may want to consult a tax
advisor before you elect any distribution from the plan.

Minimum Distribution Requirement

You will be required by law to take a minimum distribution of your account by April 1 of the calendar year
following the year in which you reach age 72 or retire, whichever is later. All of the plan's forms of payment meet
the minimum distribution requirement. Minimum distributions are not eligible to be rolled over into an IRA or

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 103
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

another tax-qualified retirement plan. If you do not make a timely election, you will be paid in the normal form of
payment.

Assignment of Benefits

Generally, your benefits under the plan cannot be assigned, given away, transferred, or pledged in any way.
However, there are some exceptions, such as a Qualified Domestic Relations Order (QDRO). For details of this
provision, see the Legal and Administrative Information section.

Retiree Medical Benefits

This section provides information about Kaiser Permanente Washington Retiree Medical Plan (the "Retiree
Medical Plan" or the "Plan") for eligible retirees of the Kaiser Permanente Washington Region, and retirees'
eligible spouses and domestic partners.

Who Is Eligible

You may be eligible for benefits under the Retiree Medical Plan if you meet certain age and Qualifying Service
requirements. Other criteria that may affect your eligibility include:
Ě Your work location (eastern Washington/north Idaho or western Washington) at Retirement
Ě The date of your Retirement
Ě Your employment status
Ě The ZIP code in which you reside
Please note that your years of service with Kaiser Permanente, Group Health Cooperative and/or Group Health
Options, Inc., count toward this requirement. Refer to the section below to determine the exact eligibility criteria
that apply to you.

Retiree Medical Eligibility Criteria

If you retired on or after December 31, 2009, you will be eligible for retiree medical benefits if you meet the
following requirements:
Ě Age 55+ at Retirement with 12 years of Qualifying Service
Ě Not actively employed by Kaiser Permanente, GHC or GHO, or any subsidiary or affiliate
Ě Meets applicable service area residency requirements
Ě If eligible for Medicare, is enrolled in Medicare Part A and Part B, and in the Kaiser Permanente Medicare
Advantage (HMO) plan

Dependent Eligibility

If you are eligible for retiree medical benefits, you may enroll your spouse or domestic partner if he or she meets all
of the eligibility requirements below:
Ě your spouse or domestic partner is age 55 or older
Ě your spouse or domestic partner meets applicable service area requirements
Ě if he or she is eligible for Medicare, your spouse or domestic partner is enrolled in Medicare Part A and Part B
To enroll your spouse or domestic partner in the Plan, contact the KPRC. You will be required to provide
documentation to verify your spouse or domestic partner's eligibility for the Plan.

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 104
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Please Note: If your spouse or domestic partner is under age 55 when you initially enroll in the Retiree Medical
Plan, he or she may be eligible to continue the coverage that he or she had while you were actively employed under
COBRA continuation rules. You may enroll your spouse or domestic partner in the Kaiser Permanente
Washington Retiree Medical Plan at the time he or she satisfies the applicable age requirement, if you are still
enrolled in the Plan at that time.

Residency Requirements

Residency Requirements for all Retirees

Except as noted below, only individuals who maintain a permanent residence within the Kaiser Permanente
Washington Service Area are eligible for coverage under the Retiree Medical Plan. If you maintain a primary
residence outside of the Kaiser Permanente Washington Service Area for more than six months, your retiree
medical coverage will terminate, at the end of the 6th month. Written proof of residency (such as a copy of a
utility bill) may be requested at any time.
As of November 2017, the Kaiser Permanente Washington Service Area consists of the following counties--King,
Pierce, Snohomish, Skagit, Whatcom, Lewis, Thurston, Island, San Juan, Kitsap, Mason, Spokane, Whitman,
Columbia, Walla Walla, Franklin, Benton, Yakima, Kittitas, Kootenai (Idaho), and Latah (Idaho) Counties--and
portions of Grays Harbor, Lincoln, Stevens, Adams, and Pend Oreille counties.

Residency Requirements for Medicare-Eligible Retirees only

Additionally, Medicare-eligible individuals must maintain a permanent residence within the Kaiser Permanente
Medicare Advantage Washington Service Area. If you are Medicare-eligible and live (or move) outside of the
Medicare Advantage Washington Service Area, you are not eligible to enroll in the Kaiser Permanente Washington
Retiree Medical Plan.
As of November 1, 2017, the Kaiser Permanente Medicare Advantage Washington Service Area consists of the
following counties (or portions thereof) in Washington: King, Pierce, Snohomish, Skagit, Whatcom, Lewis,
Thurston, Island, San Juan, Kitsap, Spokane Counties, and portions of Mason and Grays Harbor Counties. Please
contact the Kaiser Permanente Retirement Center for questions regarding the Kaiser Permanente Washington
Medicare Advantage Service Area.
The boundaries of the Kaiser Permanente Washington Service Area and the Medicare Advantage Service Area may
change from time to time as determined by the Kaiser Permanente Washington Region in its sole discretion,
which may affect your eligibility for benefits under the Plan.

When Benefits Begin

If you enroll in the Plan immediately following your Retirement, coverage will begin on the first day of the month
following your Retirement date.
If you enroll or make a change to your coverage due to a special enrollment event, the enrollment or change
generally takes effect on the first day of the month following the occurrence of the special enrollment event.
Except in the above situations, if you enroll or make a change to your coverage during the annual open enrollment
period, the enrollment or change takes effect on January 1 of the following year.

How to Enroll

To begin retiree medical benefits, contact the KPRC at least 90 days prior to your eligibility. The KPRC will also
attempt to contact you at your last known address. It is recommended that you keep your address current with the
KPRC so that they can reach you when you are eligible to commence benefits. You must enroll according to plan
rules in order to receive retiree medical benefits.

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 105
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

1. If you are eligible for Medicare, enroll in Medicare Parts A and B by contacting the Social Security
  Administration. Visit www.medicare.gov.

2. Enroll in a retiree medical plan through the Kaiser Permanente Retirement Center (KPRC) at
  www.myplansconnect.com/kp.

3. Complete and submit the health plan enrollment form you receive in the mail. Please wait at least one week
  after you make your elections in step 2 to submit the completed form. Otherwise, you may be enrolled in the
  wrong plan.

The KPRC will provide you with additional instructions on how to commence your benefits. Your
Medicare-eligible spouse or domestic partner must follow the same steps to enroll in retiree medical benefits.
Please refer to Coordination with Medicare for more information.

Coordination with Medicare

Once you and/or your spouse or domestic partner becomes eligible for Medicare, your retiree medical coverage
will be integrated with Medicare. You and your spouse or domestic partner must enroll in all applicable parts of
Medicare (including Parts A, and B), assign all Medicare benefits to Kaiser Permanente, and enroll in the Kaiser
Permanente Washington Medicare Advantage plan. Kaiser Permanente will automatically assign your Part D for
you; a specific assignment will not be required by you. If you assign Part D coverage to another provider, Medicare
will notify Kaiser Permanente and your coverage may be terminated.
You will be responsible for paying the Medicare Part B premiums*, the Medicare Part D premiums, and any
Medicare surcharges.
Please Note: If you fail to assign Medicare to Kaiser Permanente within a 60-day grace period, your retiree
medical benefits will be terminated. During the 60-day grace period, your monthly premium cost will be
substantially higher if you are not enrolled in a Kaiser Permanente Medicare Advantage Plan. To avoid paying the
higher monthly premium during the grace period, complete the Medicare Advantage enrollment form and return
it to the address on the form so that they receive it no later than the last day of the month that precedes your
Medicare start date (or your Retiree Medical Plan start date, if you are a new enrollee who will be
Medicare-eligible upon enrollment).

Medicare Part B Premium Reimbursements

If you're eligible for reimbursement of your Medicare Part B premiums, the KPRC may require documentation
showing that you in fact paid the premium, and may condition your reimbursement upon proof of such payment.
If you are entitled to reimbursement, direct deposit of this reimbursement is available. If you want to set up direct
deposit of your reimbursement check, you have any questions about the reimbursement process, or you are unsure
whether you're eligible for reimbursement of your Medicare Part B premiums, contact the KPRC.
For information about Medicare Part B reimbursement claims and appeals, please see the Disputes, Claims and
Appeals section.
*If you retired from a Western Washington position and were at least age 55 with 12 or more years of Qualifying
Service with the Company as of January 1, 1993, the Plan reimburses you, on a quarterly basis, for Medicare Part
B premiums paid by you and your eligible spouse.

Your Retiree Medical Benefits

The Kaiser Permanente Washington Retiree Medical Plan provides comprehensive medical benefits, including:

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 106
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Ě Medical benefits
Ě Pharmacy benefits
Ě Vision exams
Ě Mental health and substance abuse benefits

Coverage options

Eligible retired staff who are not eligible for Medicare may choose from three retiree medical benefit options
within the Retiree Medical Plan, referred to as:
Ě Kaiser Permanente Washington Retiree Medical Plan 1
Ě Kaiser Permanente Washington Retiree Medical Plan 2
Ě Kaiser Permanente Washington Retiree Medical Plan 3
Once you become eligible for Medicare, you can receive coverage only under Kaiser Permanente Washington
Retiree Medical Plan 1 or Plan 4.
If you and your eligible spouse or domestic partner are not Medicare-eligible, you may select coverage under Plans
1, 2, or 3, but you must both elect the same coverage option. Once one of you becomes eligible for Medicare,
coverage for that participant is available only under Plan 1 (or Plan 4, if you were enrolled in the Washington
Permanente Medical Group Plan prior to January 1, 2017). The non-Medicare-eligible individual may elect Plan
1, 2, or 3 until he or she becomes eligible for Medicare.
The information in this section is a summary only. It does not fully describe your benefit coverage. For details on
your benefit coverage, including a complete list of benefits, services, exclusions, and limitations, as well as your
rights and responsibilities as a plan participant, refer to your Evidence of Coverage brochure (for Plans 1 and 4) or
your Benefits Booklet (for Plans 2 and 3), the binding documents between Kaiser Foundation Health Plan
(KFHP) and its members. If you have any questions or problems using your KFHP coverage, or to obtain a copy
of the Evidence of Coverage or the Benefits Booklet, please call Member Services.
Each of these plans has different out-of-pocket costs and monthly premiums. In general, Plan 1 offers the lowest
point-of-service costs (no deductible, copays or coinsurance) and out-of-pocket maximum and the highest
monthly premium, whereas Plan 3 offers the highest point-of-service costs and out-of-pocket limits and the lowest
monthly premium.

Your Monthly Premium Cost

What you pay each month for your retiree medical coverage varies depends on the plan you choose, when you
reached eligibility for retiree medical benefits, when you terminated employment, and where you retired from:
Your monthly premium cost will be the difference between the applicable employer contribution and the full
premium cost for the specific coverage option (Plan 1, Plan 2 or Plan 3) that you select.
If you are a Western Washington employee, the employer contribution is:

     - $143.68 per month for you or your surviving spouse if you are eligible for Medicare
     - $263.88 per month for you or your surviving spouse if you are not eligible for Medicare
     - $287.36 per month if both you and your spouse are enrolled and eligible for Medicare
     - $407.56 if both you and your spouse are enrolled and only one of you is eligible for Medicare
     - $573.18 per month if both you and your spouse are enrolled and neither of you are eligible for Medicare
If you were an Eastern Washington employee, the employer contribution is:

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 107
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

     - $50 per month each for you and your spouse regardless of Medicare eligibility
Premiums are subject to change annually. The current year's retiree medical premiums are available upon request
from the KPRC. Enrollees will receive updated cost information annually during open enrollment, and pay the
monthly premium to the Plan's third-party administrator, HealthEquity.

When Benefits End

Your retiree medical coverage will end as of the date any of the following occurs:
Ě If you fail to pay your monthly premium
Ě You no longer satisfy the eligibility requirements of the Plan
Ě You do not reside in the Kaiser Permanente Washington Service Area for six or more consecutive months in any

  period of 12 consecutive months
Ě You elect not to continue coverage
Ě You become eligible for Medicare but fail to enroll in and maintain enrollment in both Medicare Part A and

  Part B coverage and the Kaiser Permanente Washington Medicare Advantage plan
Ě Your death
Ě Kaiser Permanente Washington terminates the Plan, or modifies it in such a way as to terminate your coverage.
Ě You become an active employee with Kaiser Permanente in any capacity.
Coverage for your eligible spouse or domestic partner will end when your own coverage ends, or when any of the
following occurs:
Ě The first day of any month for which you or your spouse or domestic partner does not pay a required premium
Ě Your spouse or domestic partner no longer satisfies the eligibility requirements of the Plan
Ě Your spouse or domestic partner does not reside in the Kaiser Permanente Washington Service Area for six or

  more consecutive months in any period of 12 consecutive months
Ě You, or your spouse or domestic partner, elect not to continue coverage for your eligible spouse or domestic

  partner
Ě Your eligible spouse or domestic partner becomes eligible for Medicare but fails to enroll in and maintain both

  Medicare Part A and Part B coverage and the Kaiser Permanente Washington Medicare Advantage plan
Ě Your spouse or domestic partner dies
Ě Kaiser Foundation Health Plan of Washington terminates the Plan or modifies it in such a way as to terminate

  coverage for your spouse or domestic partner.

Rehired Retirees

If you retire before January 1, 2010 and are rehired into a benefited or non-benefited position with
GHC/Kaiser Permanente, your retiree medical benefits will stop while you are employed with Kaiser Permanente.
When you retire again, the benefits you are offered will be those in effect for the employee group and region from
your fist retirement.
If you retire on/after January 1, 2010 and are rehired into a benefited or non-benefited position, your retiree
medical benefits will stop while you are employed with GHC/Kaiser Permanente. When you retire again, the
benefits you are offered will be those in effect for the employee group and region from which you re-retire.

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 108
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Retiree Medical Coverage for Survivors

After You Retire

In the event of your death during retirement, your spouse or domestic partner may continue or begin benefits,
based on when you would have been eligible. Survivor benefits will end if your spouse or domestic partner
remarries or enters a new domestic partner relationship.

Before You Retire

If you die while actively employed, and after becoming eligible for retiree medical benefits, your spouse or
domestic partner/civil union partner may continue benefits (or begin benefits, based on when you would have
been eligible). Eligibility for your spouse or domestic partner/civil union partner will continue until he or she
remarries, enters a new domestic partner/civil union partner relationship, or dies.

Retiree Medical Health Reimbursement Account

Once you retire from Kaiser Permanente and you become eligible for and enroll in Medicare, you can access a
Retiree Medical Health Reimbursement Account (HRA). The Retiree Medical HRA is a notional account, which
is an account where funds are made available only when you present a reimbursement claim.

Who Is Eligible

You are eligible to participate in the Retiree Medical Health HRA if you are at least age 55 and have 15 or more
years of service at the time you retire or terminate employment. Please refer to "Qualifying Service for Retiree
Medical HRA" under the Definitions section for more details.

Retiree Medical HRA Balance

The initial balance of your Retiree Medical HRA will be based on $350 per each year of Qualifying Service with
Kaiser Permanente at retirement or termination. For example, if you retire from Kaiser Permanente with 30 years
of Qualifying Service, the initial Retiree Medical HRA balance will be $10,500.
If you were actively employed by Group Health Cooperative (GHC) and transitioned to Kaiser Permanente on
February 1, 2017, any prior service with GHC will be taken into consideration when determining your years of
Qualifying Service eligibility for the Retiree Medical HRA.
Years of Qualifying Service also applies to employees who were employed by Columbia Medical Associates (CMA)
prior to January 1, 2019, and who was hired into a position with KFHP of Washington on January 1, 2019.

How the Retiree Medical HRA Works

When you have eligible medical expenses, you submit a claim for reimbursement. When you become eligible to
access the Retiree Medical HRA, you will receive a letter that will explain how the HRA works in detail.
For more information about the Retiree Medical HRA, or to access your account, you may visit the Kaiser
Permanente Retirement Center (KPRC) website. You can also call the KPRC.

Eligible Medical Expenses

In order for expenses to be eligible for reimbursement, you must incur them while you are actively participating in
the Retiree Medical HRA.
If you live in a Kaiser Permanente Medicare Advantage Service Area, you can use the Retiree Medical HRA to be
reimbursed for expenses such as the Kaiser Permanente Medicare Advantage (HMO) plan including copayments,
deductibles, and prescription drugs, over-the-counter drugs, menstrual products, Kaiser Permanente Medicare
Advantage (HMO) plan premiums, and copayments for you and your Medicare-eligible spouse or tax-dependent

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 109
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

domestic partner. The Retiree Medical HRA can cover only medical expenses allowed under Internal Revenue
Code rules, and that are for Medicare-eligible services connected with a Kaiser Permanente medical plan.
If you live outside a Kaiser Permanente Medicare Advantage Service Area, you can use the Retiree Medical HRA to
reimburse you for your and your spouse or tax-dependent domestic partner's individual Medicare supplement plan
or Medicare Advantage plan costs, including premiums, and any deductibles, coinsurance, and copayments
associated with the Medicare supplement or Medicare Advantage plan you enroll in, in accordance with Internal
Revenue Code guidelines. You may not use the Retiree Medical HRA to pay for costs outside of a Medicare
supplement or Kaiser Permanente Medicare Advantage (HMO) plan. For example, the costs of another
employer-sponsored group health plan are not covered.

Expenses Not Covered

You cannot be reimbursed from the Retiree Medical HRA for expenses associated with any non-Kaiser Permanente
health plan, except for expenses incurred for covered services of a Medicare supplement or Medicare Advantage
plan if no Kaiser Permanente Medicare Advantage (HMO) plan is available where you live.
In addition, you cannot be reimbursed from the Retiree Medical HRA for:
Ě Expenses in excess of the Retiree Medical HRA account balance
Ě Expenses incurred before you were eligible to access the Retiree Medical HRA or while you are employed at

  Kaiser Permanente
Ě Expenses for someone that does not qualify as your dependent under the Internal Revenue Code
Ě Reimbursement for your children's health care expenses
Ě Babysitting expenses due to doctor visits
Ě Baldness treatments or hair transplants
Ě Cosmetic surgery, procedures, services, and products (non-medically necessary)
Ě Dental veneers or bonding (non-medically necessary)
Ě Dietary, nutritional and herbal supplements used to maintain general health
Ě Diet foods
Ě Electrolysis
Ě Exercise equipment or programs to promote general health
Ě Family and marriage counseling
Ě Funeral services
Ě Marijuana or other Schedule 1 controlled substances (even for medical purposes)
Ě Medical insurance premiums paid for a non-Kaiser Permanente medical plan, except as noted above, or for

  another employer's plan
Ě Medicare Part B or Part D premiums
Ě Medicare Part B or Part D surcharges, such as late enrollment surcharges and the income-related monthly

  adjustment amount
Ě Recreational lessons, such as swimming or dancing
Ě Vacation expenses (even if recommended by a doctor)
Ě Varicose vein cosmetic procedure

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 110
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Additional federal limits may apply.

How to File a Retiree Medical HRA Reimbursement Claim

For information about how to file a claim for reimbursement from the Retiree Medical HRA, and how to appeal a
denied claim, please see the Disputes, Claims, and Appeals section.

When the Retiree Medical HRA Closes

The Retiree Medical HRA will be closed and benefits terminated when any of the following conditions are met:
Ě The Retiree Medical HRA balance reaches zero ($0)
Ě Upon your death, if you have no surviving spouse or domestic partner who was an eligible dependent as defined

  in the Internal Revenue Code
Ě Upon the remarriage, recommitment, or death of your surviving spouse or eligible domestic partner

Retiree Medical HRA for Surviving Spouse or Tax-Dependent Domestic Partner

If you die before the Retiree Medical HRA balance reaches zero, any balance in the Retiree Medical HRA will be
available for your surviving spouse, or for a surviving domestic partner who was a dependent as defined by the
Internal Revenue Code, (but not for children) for eligible medical expenses.
If you die before becoming eligible to use the Retiree Medical HRA, but after you satisfied the Retiree Medical
benefit age and years of service eligibility requirements, your surviving spouse or eligible domestic partner may
access the Retiree Medical HRA when you would have reached age 65.
Your spouse or tax-dependent domestic partner's eligibility to access the HRA as a survivor will end if he or she
remarries or enters a new domestic partner relationship.

Continuation of Coverage Under COBRA

Under certain circumstances you or your eligible spouse or domestic partner covered by the Retiree Medical Plan
(Covered Dependents) have the right, under the Consolidated Omnibus Budget Reconciliation Act of 1985, as
amended (COBRA), to continue coverage under the Retiree Medical Plan ("COBRA Continuation Coverage" or
Continuation Coverage). COBRA Continuation Coverage is available to you and to Covered Dependents when
you or they would otherwise lose coverage under the Retiree Medical Plan. This section generally explains
COBRA Continuation Coverage, when it may become available to you and your spouse or domestic partner, and
what you need to do to protect the right to receive it. COBRA Continuation Coverage for the Plan is
administered by HealthEquity.

COBRA Qualifying Events

COBRA Continuation Coverage is available if you are enrolled in the Retiree Medical Plan and you and your
Covered Dependent's enrollment would otherwise end on account of a Qualifying Event. COBRA Continuation
Coverage is offered to each person who is a Qualified Beneficiary. A Qualified Beneficiary is someone who will
lose coverage under the Retiree Medical Plan because of a Qualifying Event.
Your Covered Dependent will become a Qualified Beneficiary if coverage under the Retiree Medical Plan will be
lost because any of the following Qualifying Events occur:
Ě you become divorced or legally separated from your Covered Dependent spouse; or
Ě terminate your domestic partnership with your Covered Dependent domestic partner (not followed by marriage
to the same individual).
In addition, sometimes, filing a proceeding in bankruptcy under title 11 of the United States Code can be a
Qualifying Event. If a proceeding in bankruptcy is filed with respect to the Kaiser Foundation Health Plan of

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 111
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Washington, and that bankruptcy results in the loss of coverage of any retired employee covered under the Plan,
the retired employee will become a Qualified Beneficiary with respect to the bankruptcy. The retired employee's
spouse, surviving spouse, and domestic partner will also become Qualified Beneficiaries if bankruptcy results in the
loss of their coverage under the Plan.
Please Note: Moving outside the applicable Kaiser Permanente Washington Service Area, failing to pay monthly
premium costs, or failing to enroll in or assign Medicare to Kaiser Permanente when you become eligible, is not a
Qualifying Event.
The Plan offers COBRA Continuation Coverage to Qualified Beneficiaries only after HealthEquity has been
notified that a Qualifying Event has occurred. For a divorce, legal separation or termination of domestic
partnership Qualifying Events, you or a Qualified Beneficiary must notify the KPRC in writing within 60 days
after the Qualifying Event, or if later, the date coverage under the Retiree Medical Plan is lost. The KPRC will in
turn notify HealthEquity. If you or the Qualified Beneficiary do not provide notice to KPRC within this time
period, coverage cannot be continued.
If the Qualifying Event is the commencement of bankruptcy proceedings with respect to Kaiser Foundation
Health Plan of Washington, the Plan will notify HealthEquity.
After receiving notice of a Qualifying Event, HealthEquity will either notify the Qualified Beneficiaries of their
right to elect Continuation Coverage or, if it determines that they are not entitled to COBRA Continuation
Coverage, send them a notice explaining the reasons the coverage is unavailable.

How to Obtain COBRA Coverage

Your covered spouse or domestic partner will be provided with a COBRA election form, which they must fill out
and return within 60 days of the notification date shown on the form, or loss of coverage date, if later. If they do
not return the form within 60 days of the notification date or the loss of coverage date, if later, HealthEquity will
assume that coverage has been declined.
If HealthEquity is not notified within 60 days of the qualifying event, COBRA rights will be forfeited. Contact
HealthEquity for additional information.
If your qualified beneficiary chooses COBRA Continuation Coverage, Kaiser Permanente will provide coverage
that is identical to the coverage that was in effect under the Retiree Medical Plan on the day before the Qualifying
Event.
If your qualified beneficiary initially waives COBRA Continuation Coverage, he or she can still elect COBRA
coverage before the end of the 60-day election period. Once the election period expires, however, the qualified
beneficiary will not be able to elect COBRA coverage.

Cost of COBRA Coverage

If your qualified beneficiary elects COBRA coverage, he or she will be charged the full cost of the applicable
premium, plus a 2 percent administrative fee. "Applicable premium" refers to the full cost of the overage, without
any contribution by Kaiser Permanente. Kaiser Permanente does not contribute to COBRA Continuation
Coverage. Premium rates are subject to change annually.
Payments for COBRA Continuation overage are due monthly on the first day of the month. The Qualified
Beneficiary must make the first payment within 45 days after the date coverage is elected. The first payment will
include the cost of coverage retroactive to the date coverage would otherwise terminate. Subsequent payments
must be made within 30 days of the date due or continuation coverage will be terminated as of the end of the last
month for which payment was made.

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 112
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Duration of Continuation of Coverage under COBRA

The maximum duration of COBRA continuation coverage is 36 months. Once the qualified beneficiary has paid
the initial premium, coverage is retroactive to the date the previous coverage ended. In no event will Continuation
Coverage extend more than 36 months beyond the date of the original qualifying event.

When Coverage Ends

The 36-month COBRA coverage period described above is the maximum coverage period. COBRA coverage will
end automatically before the end of the maximum period for any of the following reasons:
Ě Kaiser Foundation Health Plan ceases to provide any retiree medical plans
Ě Thirty days after a premium payment is due, if a Qualified Beneficiary fails to pay the applicable COBRA

  premiums on time
Ě The Qualified Beneficiary becomes covered, after electing COBRA coverage, under another Kaiser Permanente

  plan that does not contain any exclusions or limitations for pre-existing conditions that affect the qualified
  beneficiary
Ě The Qualified Beneficiary becomes entitled to Medicare after electing COBRA Continuation Coverage (for
  these purposes, a qualified beneficiary is not considered to be "entitled" to Medicare until he or she has actually
  completed the Medicare enrollment process with the Social Security Administration and has been notified that
  his or her Medicare coverage is in effect).
If COBRA Continuation Coverage ends before the maximum coverage period, HealthEquity will send a notice of
early termination as soon as feasible after the decision to terminate the coverage.

Plan Changes

During the time your Qualified Beneficiary has COBRA coverage, there may be changes to the applicable retiree
medical coverage option, such as new deductibles, changes to covered expenses, or to your premium. Any changes
to the retiree medical coverage option will also apply to COBRA Continuation Coverage for that coverage option.

Additional Details

COBRA coverage will be provided as required by law. If the law changes, your rights will change accordingly. For
more information on COBRA continuation coverage, rights, and obligations, contact HealthEquity.

Definitions

Full-Time Employee
For employment as of March 1, 1987, a Full-Time Employee is defined as an individual who was employed by
Group Health Cooperative, Inc. or subsequently by the Kaiser Permanente Washington Region and classified on
the employer's personnel records as 30 hours or above; and
For employment prior to March 1, 1987, an individual who was employed by Group Health Cooperative, Inc.
and classified on the employer's personnel records as 40 hours.
Qualifying Service for the Retiree Medical Plan and Retiree Medical HRA
Qualifying Service for the Retiree Medical Plan and Retiree Medical HRA is defined as periods of employment in
accordance with the policies and practices of the employer, including, without limitation, the following:

                                      KPWA | SEIU Healthcare 1199NW | January 2021 | Page 113
                                        RETIREMENT PROGRAMS

Ě Periods of employment while an individual is employed as a Full-Time Employee in a Regular Position
Ě Periods during which an employee was on an authorized paid leave of absence
Ě Periods of employment with Group Health Cooperative (GHC) before February 1, 2017, only for an Employee

  who was employed by GHC on January 31, 2017 and who became a KFHP of Washington employee on
  February 1, 2017 as part of the GHC acquisition
Ě Periods of employment with Columbia Medical Associates (CMA) before January 1, 2019, only for an
  Employee who was employed by CMA on December 31, 2018 and who was hired into a position with KFHP
  of Washington on January 1, 2019
The following do not count toward calculating Qualifying Service:
Ě Fractional years
Ě Periods of continuous employment when an Employee is classified as 0.74 FTE (or less) in a Regular Position
Ě Periods of employment during which an Employee was on an unpaid leave of absence
Ě Periods of employment with KPS Health Plans before January 1, 2012
Regular Position
A position with the employer that is considered a benefits-eligible position.

Service for Leased Employees

If you provided services to Kaiser Permanente as an employee of a leasing company (that is, a third party provider
of employee services) for at least 12 months before or after working as a regular employee, Kaiser Permanente's
retirement plans may recognize additional service (for the limited purposes described below) for time you worked
at Kaiser Permanente through the leasing company. To qualify for this additional service, you must submit
sufficient evidence that you performed work at Kaiser Permanente for at least 1,500 hours during a 12-month
period, and that while employed by the leasing company during this period, your services were subject to Kaiser
Permanente's direction and control.
Service granted on the basis of employment with a leasing company can count toward:
Ě Defined contribution plan vesting (if applicable)
Ě Eligibility for employer contributions under defined contribution plans (if applicable)
Ě Eligibility for participation in employer matching contributions (if applicable) to a tax-deferred retirement

  savings plan
Any service granted under this program will NOT count toward:
Ě Retiree Medical and any other retiree health and welfare plan eligibility
Ě Other Kaiser Permanente programs (such as vacation)
For information about how to make a request to recognize such service, please contact the Kaiser Permanente
Retirement Center (KPRC).

Disputes, Claims, and Appeals

This section of the SPD describes the dispute process and how to file a claim for your health and welfare
retirement benefits, retirement savings benefits, and/or retirement health benefits. In addition, you will find
information on how to appeal a benefit claim determination.
